  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_6cd162de-7956-4a02-9ea2-2e200f46e5ed'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

  <span id="freeText112058493074135911" style="display:none">He is <b>DRUSS the Legend</b>. His skill in battle has earned him a fearsome reputation throughout the world and the stories of his life are told everywhere. But the grizzled veteran has spurned a life of fame and fortune and has retreated to the solitude of his mountain lair to await his old enemy, Death.<br /><br />Meanwhile, barbarian hordes of the Nadir are on the march, conquering all before them. All that stands before them and victory is the legendary six-walled fortress of the Drenai empire, Dros Delnoch. If the fortress falls, so do the Drenai. Druss reluctantly agrees to come out of retirement. But can even Druss live up to his own legends?<br /><br />Held by many to be Gemmell's most iconic work, the book is considered a classic in the heroic fantasy genre.</span>

<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/121989-do-i-have-to-read-his-drenai-series-in">Do I have to read his Drenai series in order, or can i read them in any order?
Furthermore, if i only read Legend, is that a stand alone novel... or must i read on?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_121989'><a id="like_count_community_question_121989" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/121989?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">3 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F618177.Legend">like</a></span>

<span class='communityAnswererName'>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">3 years late, but it will help others wondering the same thing as you. The published order is best and the general consensus seems to be that Gemmell <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">3 years late, but it will help others wondering the same thing as you. The published order is best and the general consensus seems to be that Gemmell wrote them in the order they should be read . You'll find the writing quality all over the place if you read chronologically. I recently made this to help compare chronology vs published order: <a href="https://theexplorationjournal.files.wordpress.com/2018/06/drenai-v2.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">Drenai Saga reading order</a><a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5201603165739960984">I never read any David Gemmell until I was already published. And even then, he first came to my attention after someone e-mailed me, saying something along the lines of, "I'm glad someone like you is here to carry on Gemmell's tradition now that he's dead..." <br/><br/>After I got a few more e-mails along a similar line, I went out and bought Legend, read it, and was terribly flattered by the comparison. <br/><br/>Since then, I've actually won the Gemmell award. Which is flattering in its own right. Plus awesome, </span>
  <span id="freeText5201603165739960984" style="display:none">I never read any David Gemmell until I was already published. And even then, he first came to my attention after someone e-mailed me, saying something along the lines of, "I'm glad someone like you is here to carry on Gemmell's tradition now that he's dead..." <br /><br />After I got a few more e-mails along a similar line, I went out and bought Legend, read it, and was terribly flattered by the comparison. <br /><br />Since then, I've actually won the Gemmell award. Which is flattering in its own right. Plus awesome, because the award is an actual AXE. <br /><br />Here's a link to the blog I wrote about it, with pictures. <br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://blog.patrickrothfuss.com/2012/10/being-a-winner/">http://blog.patrickrothfuss.com/2012/...</a><br /><br />Anyway, I just re-read this, and I enjoyed it every bit as much the second time around. It's much more action oriented than my books.... <br /><br />So... yeah. Highly recommended. Especially if you like stories about what it means to be a hero. <br /></span>

<div id="review_417198057" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/417198057" />
    <a title="Kyle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11665678-kyle"><img alt="Kyle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1362814696p2/11665678.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/417198057?book_show_action=true">Sep 18, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kyle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kyle" href="/user/show/11665678-kyle">Kyle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11665678-kyle?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer417198057" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5577220615469263496"> The quality of a book is generally judged by the words in it, in addition to the story. It's not just what you say, how you say it also matters.<br/><br/> If not a complete counter example, Legend is a book where the rule loses its effect. Legend is certainly not the best written book ever, but it is most definitely one of the best books ever written. <br/><br/> David Gemmell never finished school, since he was expelled at the age of sixteen, and the unrefined writing is apparent throughout the book. He struggled </span>
  <span id="freeText5577220615469263496" style="display:none"> The quality of a book is generally judged by the words in it, in addition to the story. It's not just what you say, how you say it also matters.<br /><br /> If not a complete counter example, Legend is a book where the rule loses its effect. Legend is certainly not the best written book ever, but it is most definitely one of the best books ever written. <br /><br /> David Gemmell never finished school, since he was expelled at the age of sixteen, and the unrefined writing is apparent throughout the book. He struggled to tell his story, but he had a hell of a story to tell. What the book lacks in sophistication of wordsmithing, it more than makes up for with the raw power of the story. <br /><br /> Allow a thought experiment for the moment: Strip away all the decoration in a typical book, all the character action/interaction that exists for flavor, all the worldbuilding, all the prose, exposition, and clever tropes. What are we left with? Usually very little. Usually a basic plot, that we're lucky to even partially connect with. It might even be an intelligent story, or an imaginative one. But it's ultimately weak, skeletal, and insignificant in almost every way. It might even be non-existent. <br /><br /> Luckily, our world has been gifted with a book like Legend where we can prove such a thought experiment wrong. Strip away the decoration and frosting from Legend; cut it down to its most basic elements, and we are still left with a book worthy of the test of time.<br /><br /> In the Iliad, Achilles was given a choice by the gods: To live a short, glorious, heroic life that will end violently but be remembered, or to live a long, healthy life and eventually suffer the fading effect of time upon his name. We all know what choice Achilles made, and Achilles is remembered as one of the greatest heroes ever to come from the ranks of humanity. <br /><br /> In his own way Druss, the main character in Legend, faced the same choice. Fade into old age and senility, or face down your death with defiance at the cost of a shorter lifespan.<br /><br /> Yet Achilles is not the only hero who is remembered through the ages. In fact, the greatest hero of the Iliad is Hector. Where Achilles is remembered for the glory of his life, Hector is heroic for the manner of his death. Knowing with absolute certainty that to face Achilles in a duel means death, he accepts the challenge anyway. Not to be suicidal, but to die in the manner he tried to live. What makes a man (or woman) great, or heroic? What does it mean to die a "good death?" For that matter, what does it mean to even live a life worth living? <br /><br /> Overcoming great obstacles and succeeding is not compelling enough. Fighting, failing, and dying knowing that your name will be remembered isn't even heroic enough. The true hero, is the one who fights against that which he knows he cannot possibly defeat. Not for the remembrance of his name, or the glory of his cause, but for himself. Humans often die for one another. A mother takes a gang member's bullet to save her child, a man on life-support wants the plug pulled so his heart can be transplanted to save another, or a soldier dives upon a grenade to save his squad mates. What makes one case more heroic than the next? What if nobody was around to recognize such sacrifice?<br /><br /> If the mother knows with certainty that jumping to take the bullet will still not save the child from death, yet does it anyway, is it still heroic, or foolish? If nobody is to witness that mother's sacrifice, should it affect her decision to commit it? If nobody pulls the man's life-support plug for him, but in a rare act of clarity he manages to pull it himself while he is alone in his hospital room, does it detract from the glory or worthiness of his death? If the foxhole of soldiers becomes surrounded by an insurmountable enemy, and if the soldier knows without a doubt that diving upon the grenade will not save his friends from the battle. Should he do it anyway? No one will know he did such a thing. <br />No medal will be given, nor monument raised to his name.<br /><br /> What makes a death a good death? And what makes a life worth living?<br /><br /> The characters of Legend are the characters within us all. Fear, doubt, and futility are all present, but so too are the traits which make us greater than the sum of our parts. Honor, courage, duty, and yes, even love are all necessary components for a heroic tale of such resonance. <br /><br /> David Gemmell wrote Legend, as he was waiting to find out whether or not he was going to die from cancer, and it is his attempt at dealing with mortality. What does it mean to die well, or live well? What does it mean to be a man? Is love even worth the effort if it is destined to last only a brief moment and end in pain? <br /><br /> Socrates said the unexamined life is not worth living, but perhaps the unexamined death is not worth dying either. All life leads to death, but perhaps all death should be embraced with the joys of life.<br /><br /> Very few books have had an impact comparable to Legend, and as I said, for all it's technical flaws it is one of the finest novels ever written. Gemmell's fears are my fears. His hopes, my hopes. Legend was his first and greatest book, and its very existence makes the world a fuller place, and humanity wealthier. <br /><br /> <br /><br /><br /><br /> R.I.P, Mr. Gemmell, you've earned it.<br /><br /> <br /><br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="5577220615469263496" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_84769279" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/84769279" />
    <a title="Ahmad Sharabiani" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/614778-ahmad-sharabiani"><img alt="Ahmad Sharabiani" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1194930432p2/614778.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/84769279?book_show_action=true">Jan 13, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ahmad Sharabiani" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ahmad Sharabiani" href="/user/show/614778-ahmad-sharabiani">Ahmad Sharabiani</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9789648944518" href="/book/show/7556031">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/614778-ahmad-sharabiani?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/614778-ahmad-sharabiani?shelf=epic">epic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/614778-ahmad-sharabiani?shelf=war">war</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/614778-ahmad-sharabiani?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/614778-ahmad-sharabiani?shelf=20th-century">20th-century</a>,

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer84769279" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17474683695903389023">A Legend Book = Legend (The Drenai Saga #1), David Gemmell<br/><br/><b>Legend</b>, published in 1984, is the first and most famous novel of British fantasy writer David Gemmell. It established him as a major fantasy novelist and created the character of Druss, who would appear in several subsequent books. It was also the first novel in The Drenai saga. <br/>The Drenai Empire is under threat. The tribal Nadir people have been united for the first time by the great warleader Ulric, who has forged a massive empire in th</span>
  <span id="freeText17474683695903389023" style="display:none">A Legend Book = Legend (The Drenai Saga #1), David Gemmell<br /><br /><b>Legend</b>, published in 1984, is the first and most famous novel of British fantasy writer David Gemmell. It established him as a major fantasy novelist and created the character of Druss, who would appear in several subsequent books. It was also the first novel in The Drenai saga. <br />The Drenai Empire is under threat. The tribal Nadir people have been united for the first time by the great warleader Ulric, who has forged a massive empire in the North. The Drenai leader Abalayn is trying to negotiate new treaties with Ulric, but war is brewing and an over 500,000 strong Nadir army marches on the fortress of Dros Delnoch, gateway to the Drenai heartlands. Dros Delnoch is the greatest fortress in the world, a narrow pass guarded by six high walls and a great keep, but under Abalayn its complement of defenders has been reduced to less than 10,000 men under the leadership of an unfit General. The fate of the Drenai hinges on the defence of Dros Delnoch. If the fortress can hold the Nadir horde for three months, the Drenai general Magnus Woundweaver might be able to gather and train a Drenai army. However, given the odds, no-one truly believes that Delnoch can be held. ...<br /><br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: ماه سپتامبر سال 2009 میلادی<br /><br />عنوان: اسطوره؛ نویسنده: دیوید گمل؛ مترجم: سهیلا فرزین نژاد؛ تهران، تندیس، 1388؛ در 482 ص؛ شابک: 9789648944518؛ موضوع داستانهای افسانه و اسطوره ای از نویسندگان انگلیسی - سده 20 م<br /><br />دراس، فرمانده تبر: داستان زندگی او همه جا دهان به دهان بازگو میشود. به جای ثروت و شهرتی که میتوانست طلب کند، ملکی کوهستانی را برگزیده بود، زمینی تنها، دورافتاده و بلند، که به ابرها سر میسایید. آن بالا جنگجوی پیر سپیدمو، همنشین پلنگ برفی بود؛ و چشم انتظار مرگ دشمن خود؛<br /><br />نقل از متن کتاب: «سرآغاز: پیک درنای با حالتی عصبی بیرون درهای بزرگ تالار فرمانروایی که توسط دو نگهبان نادیر حفاظت میشد، منتظر بود؛ نگهبانها به روبرو خیره شده بودند، چشمان کشیده و اریب آنها به نشان عقاب برنزی نصب شده بر روی در چوبی تیره رنگ، دوخته شده بود. لبان خشک خود را با زبان خشکش لیسید و شنل بنفش رنگش را بر روی شانه های استخوانیش مرتب کرد. آنروز در اتاق شورا، در درنان، در فاصله ی نهصد کیلومتری سمت جنوب، هنگامیکه آبالاین از او خواست که این ماموریت مهم و حساس را به عهده بگیرد، با چه اطمینان و اتکا به نفسی ماموریت را پذیرفته بود. ماموریت سفر به گلگوتیر و گرفتن تائید و تصویب عهدنامه ای با اولریک، ارباب قبایل نادیر. در گذشته، بارتلوس در تهیه ی پیش نویس عهدنامه کمک کرده بود و دوبار هم در هنگام مذاکره در واگریای غربی و در سمت جنوب در ماشراپور حضور داشت. تمام مردم ارزش و اهمیت تجارت و لزوم احتراز از اقداماتی مخرب و هزینه بر همچون جنگ را به خوبی میدانستند. به یقین اولریک هم از این قاعده مستثنی نبود. درست است که ملل دشت شمالی را مورد یورش و چپاول قرار داده بود، اما باید به یادداشت که شمالی ها هم در طول قرنها با گرفتن خراج و مورد حمله و غارت قراردادن این مردم، خون آنها را مکیده بودند؛ ملل دشت شمالی خود بذر نابودی خویش را کاشته بودند. مردم درنای اینگونه نبودند. همیشه با احترام و شعور با مردم نادیر برخورد کرده بودند؛ شخص آبالاین دوبار در شهر خیمه ای آنها در شمال به ملاقات اولریک رفته بود ـ و پذیرایی شاهانه ای شده بود. اما بارتلوس از دیدن ویرانی و غارت در گلگوتیر سخت یکه خورده بود. دیدن اینکه دروازه های بزرگ شکسته، و از جا در آمده بودند، تعجبی نداشت، اما پس از آن شمار بسیاری از مدافعین قطع عضو شده بودند. میدان داخل قلعه ی اصلی به کپه ی کوچکی از دست انسان که در وسط آن تلنبار شده بود، فخر میفروخت؛ بارتلوس به خود لرزید و به زحمت فکرش را از آن خاطره برگرداند. سه روز او را منتظر نگاهداشته بودند، اما رفتارشان مودبانه ـ و حتی محبت آمیز بود. شنلش را دوباره مرتب کرد، میدانست که اندام لاغر و استخوانی او ابهت چندانی به جامه ی مخصوص پیک بودن او نمیدهد. دستمالی نخی را از لای کمربندش بیرون آورد و عرق را از روی سرِطاسش پاک کرد. همسرش همیشه به او هشدار میداد که هر وقت عصبی میشود سرش به طرز خیره کننده ای برق میزند. این چیزی بود که ترجیح میداد هرگز صحبتی درباره اش نشود. نگاهی زیر چشمی به نگهبانی که سمت راست او بود انداخت و لرزه ای را فرو نشاند. مرد کوتاهتر از او بود، کلاهخودی سیخ سیخی به سر داشت که حاشیه اش از پوست بز بود. سپر سینه ای از چوب لاک الکلی بسته بود و نیزه ای دندانه دندانه به دست داشت. صورتش پخ و بیرحم بود، چشمانش تیره و مورب. اگر بارتلوس میخواست شخص مناسبی برای بریدن دست کسی پیدا کند.؛ نگاهی به سمت چپ خود انداخت ـ و آرزو کرد کاش چنین کاری نکرده بود، زیرا نگهبان داشت او را نگاه میکرد. احساس خرگوشی را پیدا کرد که زیر پای قوشی در حال پرواز قرار دارد و شتابزده نگاهش را از نگهبان به عقاب برنزی روی در معطوف کرد. خداوند به او رحم کرد، انتظار به پایان رسید و درها چرخیدند و باز شدند. بارتلوس نفس عمیقی کشید و به داخل اتاق رفت. اتاق دراز بود، بیست ستون مرمری سقفی را نگاه داشته بودند که قبل از خشک شدن گچ، آبرنگ خورده بود. بر روی هر یک از ستونها مشعلی روشن قرار داشت که سایه های رقصان بدریختی روی دیوارهای پشت خود میانداختند. پای هر ستون یک نگهبان نادیر نیزه به دست ایستاده بود. چشمها ثابت به جلو خیره مانده بودند. بارتلوس پنجاه قدم روی کف مرمری شاه نشین به سوی اریکه پیش رفت؛ روی آن اولریک نشسته بود، جنگ سالار شمال. قد بلند نبود، اما قدرت از وجودش میبارید، هنگامیکه بارتلوس به وسط سالن رسید از پویایی تندوتیز مرد جا خورد. استخوان گونه ای برجسته و موهایی به رنگ نیمه شب داشت که خاص نادیرها بود، اما چشمان مورب او بنفش رنگ بود و نافذ؛ پوستی سبزه داشت، ریشی سه شاخه ظاهری شیطانی به او میداد که با گرمای لبخند مردک لو میرفت. اما چیزی که بیشتر از همه بارتلوس را تحت تاثیر قرار داد این بود که ارباب نادیر یک ردای سفید درنای را به تن داشت، نشان خانوادگی آبالاین؛ اسبی طلایی که در مقابل تاجی نقره ای روی دو سم بلند شده، بر روی آن برودری دوزی شده بود. پیک تعظیم مفصلی کرد. «آقای من، من حامل سلام و درود ارباب آبالاین، رهبر برگزیده ی مردم درنای آزاد برای شما هستم.» اولریک در جواب سرش را تکان داد و با حرکت دست اشاره کرد که ادامه بدهد. «ارباب من آبالاین پیروزی چشمگیر شما را بر شورشیان گلگوتیر صمیمانه تبریک میگوید و امیدوار است اکنون که هراس و سختی جنگ را پشت سر گذاشته اید، بتوانید عهدنامه های جدید و توافقنامه تجاری را که در سفر بسیار دلپذیری که بهار گذشته به اینجا داشتند، و با شما در میان گذاشتند، مورد توجه قرار بدهید. در اینجا نامه ای از ارباب آبالاین دارم و همین طور متن عهدنامه ها و توافقنامه ها.» بارتلوس قدمی پیش گذاشت، سه طومار را جلو برد. اولریک آنها را گرفت و آهسته روی زمین در کنار پایه ی اریکه گذاشت. گفت: «ممنونم، بارتلوس. بگو ببینم، آیا در میان ساکنین درنای این وحشت وجود داره که سپاه من به دروس دلنوچ لشکرکشی خواهد کرد؟» «شوخی می کنید، آقای من؟» اولریک با قیافه ای حق به جانب و معصومانه گفت: «نه، اصلاً.» صدایش بم و طنین دار بود. «تجار به من میگن که بحثهای زیادی در درنان هست.» بارتلوس گفت: «از اون حرفهایی که برای سرگرمی میزنن. من خودم در نوشتن این توافقنامه ها کمک کردم و سهیم بودم و اگر ابهامی در بعضی از مواد و بندهای اونها وجود داشته باشه، برای من افتخاره که بتونم کمک بکنم.» اولریک گفت: «نه. مطمئنم که اونها درست هستن و همه چیز روبراهه. اما تشخیص میدین که کاهن من نوستا خان باید نشانه ها رو بررسی کنه. یک رسم بدوی و عقب افتاده است، میدونم، اما اطمینان دارم که میفهمین. درسته؟» بارتلوس گفت: «البته. این چیزها تشریفات آیینی هستن.» اولریک دستهایش را دوباره برهم زد و از میان سایه های سمت چپ پیرمردی خشک و چروکیده با نیم تنه ای کثیف از پوست بز وارد شد. زیر بازوی راست لاغرش جوجه ای سفیدرنگ داشت و در دست چپش یک کاسه ی چوبی دهن گشاد و کم عمق. نزدیک که شد، اولریک برخاست و ایستاد، دستانش را پیش برد و گردن و پاهای جوجه را گرفت؛ اولریک آهسته و آرام آن را بالای سرش برد ـ سپس در مقابل چشمان وحشت زده و گشاد بارتلوس، پرنده را پایین آورد و دندانهایش را در گردن حیوان فرو برد و سر جوجه را با دندان از بدنش جدا کرد.»؛ پایان نقلو ا. شربیانی</span>
  <a data-text-id="17474683695903389023" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1748677484" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1748677484" />
    <a title="Bookwraiths" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14716035-bookwraiths"><img alt="Bookwraiths" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1353765210p2/14716035.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1748677484?book_show_action=true">Oct 21, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bookwraiths" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bookwraiths" href="/user/show/14716035-bookwraiths">Bookwraiths</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14716035-bookwraiths?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14716035-bookwraiths?shelf=own">own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1748677484" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7949400016783341105">Originally reviewed at <a href='https://bookwraiths.com/2016/10/21/flashback-friday-legend/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Bookwraiths</a> .<br/><br/>David Gemmell might not have invented action adventure fantasy, but he refined it, polished it up, and presented his updated version (<i>Against the Horde/Legend</i>) in 1984 to a reading audience who loved every minute of it. Luckily, I was one of those readers back in the 1980s; this book instantly becoming one of my favorite fantasy stories for years to come. But when I re-read it a few weeks ago, I have to admit being concerned it would not live up to my memories</span>
  <span id="freeText7949400016783341105" style="display:none">Originally reviewed at <a href="https://bookwraiths.com/2016/10/21/flashback-friday-legend/" rel="nofollow noopener">Bookwraiths</a> .<br /><br />David Gemmell might not have invented action adventure fantasy, but he refined it, polished it up, and presented his updated version (<i>Against the Horde/Legend</i>) in 1984 to a reading audience who loved every minute of it. Luckily, I was one of those readers back in the 1980s; this book instantly becoming one of my favorite fantasy stories for years to come. But when I re-read it a few weeks ago, I have to admit being concerned it would not live up to my memories; my fear that all the years since its release having muted the pulse-pounding, adrenaline rush and relegated another classic fantasy into a fallen favorite. But, thankfully, my fears were unfounded: <i>Legend</i> still as good as ever.<br /><br />Here the Nadir hordes (Think Mongols) have been united under the charismatic, intelligent, and ruthless Ulric, who determines it is time for his people to conquer their more settled neighbors, the Drenai. Standing in the way of this unstoppable barbarian force is the undermanned mountain fortress of Dros Delnoch, which should be impenetrable IF defended by an adequate force. And that is exactly what the Drenai are lacking, as the fortress is undermanned, unprepared, and without adequate commanders to inspire the troops to hold until a relief force can arrive.<br /><br />Enter Druss the Legend; he who is also known as the Captain of the Ax, the Axman, Deathwalker, and the Silver Slayer. This fearsome warrior might be past his prime, but he is determined to answer his kingdom’s desperate call, to hold Dros Delnoch until the Nadir are turned back or every warrior lies dead beneath their swords. This hero determined to finally find a death worthy of his legend!<br /><br />Joining Druss upon the battlements of Dros Delnoch are a diverse cast of characters. Rek the Baresarker and his beloved Virae come there to fight. Serbitar and the mythical order he is part of arrive to aid in the last stand of the Drenai people. Ordinary men stand side-by-side with rich commanders and wanted outlaws. All these diverse individuals inspired by Druss himself to stand up for what they believe in, sacrifice themselves in order to keep what they cherish safe from harm, and lay down their lives die before they betray that which they hold dear.<br /><br />Whenever I describe this book to a friend who is thinking of reading it, I say <i>Legend</i> is the fantasy equivalent of the Alamo, where men sacrificed their lives for a cause. And in David Gemmell’s tale of sacrifice, each of the warriors portrayed — from Druss down to the lowest soldier upon the walls — knows their mission is a suicidal one. Their forces no match for the Nadir horde. Reinforcements not able to reach them in time. Death the only real outcome of their bravery. But even knowing this, these brave men and women refuse to lay down their arms and surrender to the inevitable. They come together, find peace within themselves, lock strong arms with one another, and stand as a human walls between the world they love and those who would seek to destroy it.<br /><br />Damn, I get teary just typing all that. Honestly, I do. No matter his limitation as a writer (because I know some readers find his writing simplistic in many ways), Gemmell uses his stereotypical cast of characters to maximum effect, their words and deeds inspirational, moving, and sorrowful. Vile people finding redemption. Cowards exhibiting courage. Lawless individuals displaying extreme honor. Each heroic death cutting like a stab wound to the heart. The final stand of Druss as emotional charged and awe inspiring as any in literature.<br /><br /><i>Legend</i> might not have been groundbreaking or innovative when it was published, much less now. It doesn’t try to subvert tropes. It doesn’t attempt to present an ultra-realistic story. It doesn’t overwhelm with its exquisite prose. What is does is tell an action-packed fantasy tale of a desperate last stand of a civilization by individuals caught up in events. The tale of these people’s plight awe-inspiring and emotionally charged. In other words, <i>Legend</i> is a masterpiece of heroic fantasy, one which rightly deserves its fame even today.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7949400016783341105" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1577771334" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1577771334" />
    <a title="Mayim de Vries" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50424456-mayim-de-vries"><img alt="Mayim de Vries" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560508357p2/50424456.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1577771334?book_show_action=true">Mar 12, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mayim de Vries" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mayim de Vries" href="/user/show/50424456-mayim-de-vries">Mayim de Vries</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1577771334" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer407804911586996868"><b>There is something unambiguously alluring about last stands</b>; those situations in which a body of troops holds a defensive position in the face of overwhelming odds and against all hope for victory. We all know the battle of Thermopile 480 BC when a Greek force of approximately 7,000 men for seven days (including three of battle) held off the Persian army, alleged by the ancient sources to have numbered over one million. Less known, but not less impressive, is the Battle of Hodów between the King</span>
  <span id="freeText407804911586996868" style="display:none"><b>There is something unambiguously alluring about last stands</b>; those situations in which a body of troops holds a defensive position in the face of overwhelming odds and against all hope for victory. We all know the battle of Thermopile 480 BC when a Greek force of approximately 7,000 men for seven days (including three of battle) held off the Persian army, alleged by the ancient sources to have numbered over one million. Less known, but not less impressive, is the Battle of Hodów between the Kingdom of Poland and the Crimean Khanate forces, fought in June 1694 with four hundred hussars fighting (and winning!) against forty thousand Tatars (Now, the Poles are crazy altogether as they have their own list of last stands featuring things like the Battle of Wizna in 1939 when between 350 and 720 Poles defended a fortified line for three days against more than 40,000 Germans!). <b>Battles like these easily become legends.</b><br /><br /><b>David Gemmel gives us the legend of Dross Delnoch</b>, a strong keep with six walls defended by ten thousands men of whom most are untrained volunteers, about to withstand an attack of the greatest army ever assembled; a horde that within twenty years had built an empire stretching across a dozen lands and five score cities. And now as they march on Dross, the greatest fortress ever built is waiting for the largest army in the world. <br /><br />What a clash of giants! The ingredients for a new legend.<br /><br />Only things are not going great in the fortress. <b>There are six walls and a town to defend, while the force is less than a third of the full complement, and the discipline is rotten because morale is low and fear is rife.</b> The defenders need a miracle or the Dross will fall. And <b>Dross Delnoch needs heroes. Badly.</b><br /> <br /><i>”Think of the men here as a rusty weapon which needs a warrior’s firm hand. It needs to be sharpened, honed, prepared. It’s useless else.”</i><br /><br />Contrary to your expectations, the book doesn’t start in the city preparing for a siege. <b>The book opens with a coward running away from battle</b>, one Regank the Wanderer, <i>”man of uncertain character and only sporadic courage”</i>. In fact, the actual fighting starts only halfway through the book and <b>even though the novel is not long, there is not one word wasted. A great reminder to many contemporary writers that epic does not automatically equate with +600 pages.</b> That you can have 350 pages filled with action to the brim.<br /><br />So how does Gemmel manage to achieve it? Firstly, he creates <b>a compelling set of characters. And I would say the Legend is one of those novels that do not really have a main protagonist</b>. Surely, <b>invincible Druss</b>, Captain of the Axe, wielding Snaga (meaning “the Sender”), the greatest warrior of the age, <b>is one of the book’s main pillars but you’d be very mistaken to think that the book is about him</b>. Others are equally important in the Legend: from Rek, a hero by necessity, to Bowman, a robber outlaw with principles, from Virae, earl’s daughter, to deadly Caessa whose love is as lethal as her arrows, from Orrin, the incompetent gan of the fortress and Hogun, the grim legion general, to rank and file soldiers whom we meet, learn their back stories and accompany in battle. There is, finally, the Temple of Thirty, warrior-priests for whom the incoming battle is the culmination of thirteen years of training. They are weapon masters who seek the perfect death to counterpoint the perfect life, whose bodies are the living weapons and minds fight as powerfully but whose spirits adhere to extreme pacifism. I am sure that all readers interested in Eastern spirituality fill find the albino Serbitar one of the most fascinating characters in fantasy.<br /><br /><i>”Druss is every man who has refused to quit, to surrender when life offered no hope, to stand aside when the alternative was to die. He is a man who has shown other men there is no such thing as guaranteed defeat.”</i><br /><br />Secondly, what Gemmel shows is that <b>there is more to battle than hacking and slashing at the incoming enemy</b>. He builds the tension surrounding the incoming class and even before the fighting starts he shows the reader that <b>victory is not merely the question of military might</b>. That there is tactic and organisation to be considered; the supply lines, the orderlies, hospitals and stretcher bearers. And above all, he emphasises the role of spirit. He shows <b>the whole dynamic of the battle so beautifully captured and symbolised in how each of the walls is named</b>: Firstly, “Eldibar” which means “exultation”, followed by “Musif” the wall of despair and Kania, the wall of renewed hope. The fourth wall is named Sumitos, the wall of desperation, while Valteri, wall five, is the wall of “serenity” and, finally, Geddon is the wall of death. You will follow the defenders through these walls and through their own battles that each has to wage. <b>Because there is not one battle, but many.</b> Gemmel paints dozens of tiny pictures of deeds of individual heroism passed unseen but also shows how low a human spirit can sink during wartime with treachery, cowardice, and denial. <br /><br />Finally, while you will find the motif of good forces with all the odds pitched against them fighting the incoming evil in other heroic fantasy books (including those penned by Gemmel <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2153684783?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">himself</a>), I think that the Legend is more mature because it is more nuanced. <b>The main theme is not the clash of light against the dark</b>, good against the evil (Ulric of the Nadir is not a primitive brute but an enemy worthy of respect). The Legend invites us to ponder about the human nature, <b>the mysteries of human soul that propel us to fight for lost causes and refuse to yield even if giving up seems to be the most reasonable course of action</b>. Even if the only thing we can offer is our meaningless and unnecessary death. <br /><br /><b>Regarding my rating</b>: I approach this book in a very similar manner to the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1484918749?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Dragonlance Chronicles</a>. There is a lot of <b>nostalgia factor involved</b>. The Legend gets the benefit of being a classic and so I ignore the things that under normal circumstances would bring the final verdict down by two stars <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[mainly Ulric’s purple (!) eyes and the fact that what dies doesn’t stay dead <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br /><br />---<br />Also in The Drenai Saga: <br /><br />2. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2305679740?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">The King Beyond the Gate</a> ★★☆☆☆<br />3. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2336920559" rel="nofollow noopener">Waylander</a> ★★★☆☆<br />4. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2372503520" rel="nofollow noopener">Quest for Lost Heroes</a> ★★★★☆<br />5. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2407425852" rel="nofollow noopener">In the Realm of the Wolf</a> ★★★☆☆<br />6. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2431984941?type=review#rating_170330840" rel="nofollow noopener">The First Chronicles of Druss the Legend</a> ★★★★☆<br />7. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2470949369" rel="nofollow noopener">The Legend of Deathwalker</a> ★★★★☆<br />8. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2517328446?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Winter Warriors</a> ★★★☆☆<br />9. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2621547766" rel="nofollow noopener">Hero in the Shadows</a> ★★★★★<br />10. White Wolf RTC<br />11. The Swords of Night and Day RTC</span>
  <a data-text-id="407804911586996868" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2017977516" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2017977516" />
    <a title="Choko" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27962805-choko"><img alt="Choko" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1475642755p2/27962805.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2017977516?book_show_action=true">Jan 20, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Choko" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Choko" href="/user/show/27962805-choko">Choko</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11720877-legend">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27962805-choko?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2017977516" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13226613903582046560"><b>*** 4.44 ***<br/><br/>A buddy read with the Fantasy Buddy Reads Group, because we love the Epics!!!</b><br/><br/>And even though it barely reached 350 pages, this gem is a true Epic! It was written in the 80's and has some of the marks of its time, which coming from me is a complement, of course, being a product of the generation which came to age at that time. I find it interesting, that the books I love most, are always somehow connected with war. The authors do a great job painting the fear, loss, and horror with th</span>
  <span id="freeText13226613903582046560" style="display:none"><b>*** 4.44 ***<br /><br />A buddy read with the Fantasy Buddy Reads Group, because we love the Epics!!!</b><br /><br />And even though it barely reached 350 pages, this gem is a true Epic! It was written in the 80's and has some of the marks of its time, which coming from me is a complement, of course, being a product of the generation which came to age at that time. I find it interesting, that the books I love most, are always somehow connected with war. The authors do a great job painting the fear, loss, and horror with their words, and despite creating heroes who are shaped by the war experiences, the books are never pro-war... That is not to say they are anti-war either. However, they usually promote honor, as well as question the reasons for why humanity finds so many reasons to engage in this awful, violent, and mostly permanent solution to problems which could be dealt with in many other, more peaceful ways... <br /><br /><b>
  <i>"...“Never violate a woman, nor harm a child. Do not lie, cheat or steal. These things are for lesser men. Protect the weak against the evil strong. And never allow thoughts of gain to lead you into the pursuit of evil. Never back away from an enemy. Either fight or surrender. It is not enough to say I will not be evil. Evil must be fought wherever it is found.”The Iron Code”..."</i>
</b><br /><br />Beautiful words, but how many could say they were able to follow them? None of us are perfect and the best we can do is to try our best. One of those who has always tried his best and had some success with it is the now aging Druss, Captain of the Axe, the one called The Legend. He is a warrior of renown, the legends told of him and the songs sang have lit the spark for glory in many of children and young people's lives. Many have followed in his footsteps because of listening to his adventures and taken up the sword or axe in pale imitation of him. Most of them have found death and no songs have been written in their honor, but people tend to think of the heroes and their deeds as separate from the pain and ugliness by which they are defined.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>"...“Only a fool loves war,” said Calvar, “or a man who has never seen it. The trouble is that the survivors forget about the horrors and remember only the battle lust. They pass on that memory, and other men hunger for it.”..."</i>
</b><br /><br />Druss is called upon to inspire the soldiers and fight another last impossible to win battle, charged with holding the Dros Delnoch pass, until the Nadir Horde are repelled or every last soldier is dead. Our reluctant hero takes on the task, seeking a date with his own Death. We also have the funny, charming and very cowardly Rek, who would love to spend his life far away from any military conflict, eating drinking and keeping female company. He has a staggering fear of combat and sees this as his biggest failure. However, circumstances and a woman, contrive to take him to the middle of the biggest battle of recent times, and he has to make some hard choices. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>"...“By nature of definition only the coward is capable of the highest heroism”..."</i>
</b><br /><br /><b>
  <i>"...“A cynic by experience, a romantic by inclination and now a hero by necessity.”..."</i>
</b><br /><br />The story is about the human condition when faced with the hardest times they could possibly face. It is about what makes humans human and the fears we all live with, despite of the way others perceive us. I was very moved by some parts, others made me think of why some of us, when gone trough something rough, chose to take the path of light or darkness, are able to pick themselves up, or wallow in depression for the rest of their lives... It also made me think of how us, the regular folks, have to live with the consequences of the whims and changing moods of our leaders, who are not afraid to put our lives in danger, while quick to condemn any possible slight against their ego... But, it has be thus since the beginning of times, I guess nothing really changes, even in our Fantasy...<br /><br /><b>
  <i>"...“And what is a man? He is someone who rises when life has knocked him down. He is someone who raises his fist to heaven when a storm has ruined his crop--and then plants again. And again. A man remains unbroken by the savage twists of fate.<br /><br />That man may never win. But when he sees himself reflected, he can be proud of what he sees. For low he may be in the present scheme of things: peasant, serf, or dispossessed. But he is unconquerable”..."</i>
</b><br /><br />I will highly recommend this book and wish you enjoy the ride!!! <br /><br />I wish you all Happy Reading and many more Wonderful Books to come!!! </span>
  <a data-text-id="13226613903582046560" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17831456088354684167">An awesome BR with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/61651312-emelia-mccord' rel='nofollow noopener'>Lovely Pinky </a>and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/24111976-mikos' rel='nofollow noopener'>my fellow Catman</a>, two faithful Cat-holics.<br/><br/><b>
  <i>“Get rid of your doubts. Yesterday is dead. Past mistakes are like smoke in the breeze. What counts is tomorrow..”</i>
</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1496784781i/22952614.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I love epic fantasy <3 Fantasy books rarely let me down and “The Legend” sure didn’t. Opening such a book I look for a promise from the author, I want to dive into the rich, picturesque world, intriguing narrative, and of course gripping characters with true to life personalities (and of course with nam</span>
  <span id="freeText17831456088354684167" style="display:none">An awesome BR with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/61651312-emelia-mccord" rel="nofollow noopener">Lovely Pinky </a>and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/24111976-mikos" rel="nofollow noopener">my fellow Catman</a>, two faithful Cat-holics.<br><br><b>
  <i>“Get rid of your doubts. Yesterday is dead. Past mistakes are like smoke in the breeze. What counts is tomorrow..”</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1496784781i/22952614.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I love epic fantasy &lt;3 Fantasy books rarely let me down and “The Legend” sure didn’t. Opening such a book I look for a promise from the author, I want to dive into the rich, picturesque world, intriguing narrative, and of course gripping characters with true to life personalities (and of course with names I have difficulties to pronounce :D) That’s what I seek for in my fantasy reads 😊<br><br>Did I get this in this book? Not quite, but I can say for sure that it’s an outstanding read.<br><br>Characters. As is typical in many fantasy series, there is a big cast of characters. I liked them all, starting with Druss, a true hero, a legend, brave, strong, old and tired, but determined to die with his axe Snaga in his hand. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Virae <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, a high-born, ferocious kick-ass heroine I love meeting. And many more. They pretty much make the story. Each character has it’s role and their heroic efforts make “The Legend” an epic read. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[For example, Gan Orrin, a disrespected commander with not much strength, or Rek, an unreliable bastard. Their stories clearly show that the most ordinary of men can become legendary heroes. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><b>
  <i>“Man alone, it seems, lives all his life in the knowledge of death. And yet there is more to life than merely waiting for death. For life to have meaning, there must be a purpose. A man must pass something on -otherwise he is useless.”</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1496784781i/22952615._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Druss<br><br>Oh and the great secret and peculiar monks with an <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[albino Serbitar <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. They definitely added spices to the story not only using their great fighting skills, but also using their outstanding powers in metaphysical level. <br><br>All of them come together for what it seems a long lost battle. <br><br>Despite the strength, bravery and heroism, most of the characters don’t have much points in complexity or depth. Some make surprising developments, but sometimes their backstories or personalities are woven with simplicity. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[For example Virae, I loved following her in the first part of the book, she has potential as an independent strong woman, but in the other part of the story she was almost left to play a random role, also the insta love angle, IDK, It seemed a bit too rushed and not very real, maybe too smooth? But I confess, the ending for it just blew my mind. <br><br>I liked Bowman, the witty peculiar Robin Hood and the seductive yet troubled Caessa. Their backstories and personalities were the ones where Mr. Gemmell showed his skill in creating memorable characters.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1496784781i/22952616.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Bowman and Caessa <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Narrative. Where “The Legend” is successful, is its pacing. No long speeches or tiring descriptions, just quick pace, adventures, fighting and death! Wow, Mr. Gemmell makes Erikson proud and harvests his characters with eagerness! The story is not overly complicated, as some of the plots and sub-plots can be in long series like Malazan, but I enjoyed it nonetheless.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1496784781i/22952617._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Siege of Dros Delnoch<br><br>To sum up, I enjoyed "The Legend", and it’s really a great fantasy read. I liked the development of some characters, enjoyed the fighting and the ending was just amazing! I will read other books in the series for sure.<br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_958924145" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/958924145" />
    <a title="Conor" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30552336-conor"><img alt="Conor" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1400278909p2/30552336.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/958924145?book_show_action=true">Jun 05, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Conor" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Conor" href="/user/show/30552336-conor">Conor</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30552336-conor?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30552336-conor?shelf=gemmell">gemmell</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer958924145" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2215606653148254588">This was a masterclass in pulpy, old-school fantasy with all that entails both good and bad. The characters were fairly 1 dimensional, the world-building wasn't particularly unique or inventive and the plot was fairly straight-forward. For most books these would be criticisms and yet for this one it's almost praise: Gemmell seems entirely happy with this formula and he executes it very well. The skillful execution of these reliable tropes combined with the addition of some other nice features ma</span>
  <span id="freeText2215606653148254588" style="display:none">This was a masterclass in pulpy, old-school fantasy with all that entails both good and bad. The characters were fairly 1 dimensional, the world-building wasn't particularly unique or inventive and the plot was fairly straight-forward. For most books these would be criticisms and yet for this one it's almost praise: Gemmell seems entirely happy with this formula and he executes it very well. The skillful execution of these reliable tropes combined with the addition of some other nice features made for a really enjoyable read.<br /><br />The first 2/3 of the book were pretty well paced, characters and story elements were introduced and developed and the scene was set for the epic siege to come. The Last 1/3 or so, the duration of the siege, was where the story became really compelling. The pace picked up notably, the battle scenes provided a level of intensity that hadn't been seen before and the philosophical elements were interesting and implemented in such a way that they didn't distract from the plot (a la the bloated and repetitive philosophical monologues in the Malazan books) with most of the philosophizing coming in the brief lulls between bloody, violent clashes as the combatants try to make sense of the slaughter. <br /><br />Druss makes for an enjoyable main character. A revered old warrior who has come out of retirement for one last fight. His struggles to live up his legend even as his body failed him made for poignant reading (all the more so as Gemmell apparently had the initial idea for this while dwelling on his own mortality as he awaited the results of a cancer exam) that reminded me somewhat of Clint Eastwood's great role in Unforgiven. Rek was also a likeable protagonist: his struggles to control his berserker rages and his often comedic dialogue were all interesting features of his story. There were a cast of pretty straightforward secondary characters who all nevertheless served their roles in the story well. The standout for me was the cowardly lord of the fort. When Druss arrived a expected him to be hilarious and dramatically removed from office (with a possible pantsing/wedgie to go with it) but instead Druss gave him a second chance and his struggle to regain respect: both that of himself and of his men, was pretty inspiring.<br /><br />Overall this wasn't a groundbreaking or innovative read that made me look at the world differently, but as action-packed epic high fantasy it was a masterclass in the genre.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2215606653148254588" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_33983316" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/33983316" />
    <a title="Dan Schwent" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/870755-dan-schwent"><img alt="Dan Schwent" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593973948p2/870755.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/33983316?book_show_action=true">Sep 27, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dan Schwent" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dan Schwent" href="/user/show/870755-dan-schwent">Dan Schwent</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/870755-dan-schwent?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer33983316" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8961168801800068001">The Nadir army heads for Dros Delnoch, a keep guarding a mountain pass. Druss the Legend comes out of retirement for one last battle. But even with Rek the baresark and the earl of Delnoch's daughter help Druss and eleven thousand men stand up against an advancing army many times their size?<br/><br/>I'll be honest with you. My brother pushed this on me almost a year ago and I wasn't in a hurry to read it. I've read a few David Gemmell books before and it takes a special book to get me to read Tolkien-esq</span>
  <span id="freeText8961168801800068001" style="display:none">The Nadir army heads for Dros Delnoch, a keep guarding a mountain pass. Druss the Legend comes out of retirement for one last battle. But even with Rek the baresark and the earl of Delnoch's daughter help Druss and eleven thousand men stand up against an advancing army many times their size?<br /><br />I'll be honest with you. My brother pushed this on me almost a year ago and I wasn't in a hurry to read it. I've read a few David Gemmell books before and it takes a special book to get me to read Tolkien-esque fantasy. I've never found Gemmell's writing to be particularly good.<br /><br />While I don't find Gemmell's writing to be good, he sure knows WHAT to write. The story of Druss whipping the men into shape and the comradery that developes among the men is very moving. In fact, I choked back a couple man tears near the end. Druss's commentary on what it means to be a man is inspiring.<br /><br />Druss is like a combination of Conan the Barbarian and Clint Eastwood's character from Gran Turino. You know and he knows that his last hurrah has come. Druss knows his value as a Legend to the other soldiers at Dros Delnoch far outweighs his substantial prowess as a warrior.<br /><br />The other characters are well done as well. Ulric, leader of the Nadir, is a multi-dimensional character. It would have been easy to have him be a malevolent tyrant but he's acutally fairly likeable. Rek, Orrin, and the others also grow into their roles as the story progresses.<br /><br />I have a lot more to say but I don't want to give anything away. To sum up, this is the ultimate fantasy book for men and the women who appriciate them. Go out and get it!</span>
  <a data-text-id="8961168801800068001" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_412379394" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/412379394" />
    <a title="Evgeny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny"><img alt="Evgeny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544797852p2/9340136.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/412379394?book_show_action=true">Sep 11, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Evgeny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Evgeny" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny">Evgeny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9340136-evgeny?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer412379394" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17716911745332398341">The Drenai Empire (good guys) is threatened by barbarian horde from Nadir (not-so-good guys) where a leader emerged who managed to unite almost all the tribes and wants to conquer his neighbors. The neighbors are not prepared: they have small army and not enough competent commanders. The first fortress which happened to be in the way of barbarian contest is Dros Delnoch; if I understood correctly this is the only fortress capable of delaying the conquest of the Empire. If it falls, the rest will</span>
  <span id="freeText17716911745332398341" style="display:none">The Drenai Empire (good guys) is threatened by barbarian horde from Nadir (not-so-good guys) where a leader emerged who managed to unite almost all the tribes and wants to conquer his neighbors. The neighbors are not prepared: they have small army and not enough competent commanders. The first fortress which happened to be in the way of barbarian contest is Dros Delnoch; if I understood correctly this is the only fortress capable of delaying the conquest of the Empire. If it falls, the rest will shortly follow. <br /><br />So, on one hand we have hordes of barbarians with decent commanders; on the other hand - a very small army consisting mostly of new recruits whose task is to delay the conquerors until the reinforcements arrive (hopefully). The last hope of fortress' defenders is Druss the Legend. He is an old (and I do mean - old) warrior who defied the odds his whole life and was never defeated - think Cohen the Barbarian from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1654.Terry_Pratchett" title="Terry Pratchett" rel="nofollow noopener">Terry Pratchett</a>. So it is up to him to raise the moral and organize the defenders. <br /><br />This is fairly generic fantasy with some very minor magic. The only reason I gave this book 3 stars is Druss himself, he is a very interesting character who really makes you wish he kept defying the odds against him. If I discount Druss, the book is worth 2 stars. <br /><br />The romance between Rek and Virae (other main characters) is so badly written, I saw better in porn movies. Speaking of Rek, he undergoes completely unexplainable transformation from a coward to the bravest man in the Empire almost overnight. The epilog feels forced and not what I consider a good (or even logical) ending. I am not sure I want to read the next book in series. Can somebody inspire me to do this?</span>
  <a data-text-id="17716911745332398341" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1926004117" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1926004117" />
    <a title="Apatt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2457095-apatt"><img alt="Apatt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1349239948p2/2457095.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1926004117?book_show_action=true">Feb 26, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Apatt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Apatt" href="/user/show/2457095-apatt">Apatt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2457095-apatt?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2457095-apatt?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1926004117" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6297774939747041566"><i>“ ‘Druss the Legend. Mightiest man of his era. A killing machine, a warrior. And why? Because I never had the courage to be a farmer’, Druss told himself.<br/><br/>‘When I die’, he thought, ‘everyone will mourn for Druss the Legend. <br/>But who will mourn for <b>me</b>?’ ”</i><br/><br/>Now compare the above quotes with this famous line from the movie <a href='http://www.imdb.com/title/tt0125439/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Notting Hill</a>:<br/><br/><i>“The fame thing isn’t really real, you know. I’m also just a girl, standing in front of a boy, asking him to love her.”</i><br/><br/>Two very different kinds of story somehow conveyin</span>
  <span id="freeText6297774939747041566" style="display:none"><i>“ ‘Druss the Legend. Mightiest man of his era. A killing machine, a warrior. And why? Because I never had the courage to be a farmer’, Druss told himself.<br><br>‘When I die’, he thought, ‘everyone will mourn for Druss the Legend. <br>But who will mourn for <b>me</b>?’ ”</i><br><br>Now compare the above quotes with this famous line from the movie <a href="http://www.imdb.com/title/tt0125439/" rel="nofollow noopener">Notting Hill</a>:<br><br><i>“The fame thing isn’t really real, you know. I’m also just a girl, standing in front of a boy, asking him to love her.”</i><br><br>Two very different kinds of story somehow conveying a similar idea. One of the central themes of <i>Legend</i> is “the legend vs the man”, the difference between how people perceive you on the basis of your reputation and the actual you.<br><br>The central plotline of <i>Legend</i> concerns the invasion of The Drenai Empire by a powerful tribal nation called Nadir. In order to take over the empire, the Nadir need to break through the fortress of Dros Delnoch. The earl who runs the fortress summonses 60-year-old Druss (with his swollen knees and an arthritic back) from retirement to aid in the fortress town’s defence and to help train the military to fight against the overwhelming odds of the enormous and unstoppable Nadir force. Meanwhile, several heroic Drenai characters are also heading toward the fortress to lend their aid, all of them are aware of the impossibility of winning the war.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1488687900i/22144211._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="199" alt="Dros Delnoch" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Druss is the most vivid and larger than life character in a book full of vivid and vibrant characters. There is so much energy in his characterization that he practically leaps off the pages. He reminds me of Cohen the Barbarian from the Discworld book <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34497.The_Color_of_Magic__Discworld___1__Rincewind__1_" title="The Color of Magic (Discworld, #1; Rincewind #1) by Terry Pratchett" rel="nofollow noopener"> The Color of Magic</a>. An elderly but still deadly killing machine who is very lonely and sad underneath it all.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1488687990i/22144223._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="569" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><a href="http://lawtonlonsdale.deviantart.com/art/Druss-the-Legend-466512159" rel="nofollow noopener">Druss the Legend by LawtonLonsdale</a><br><br>In highlighting Druss I am merely scratching the surface of a very lively cast of characters, including the reluctant new earl who views himself as cowardly but automatically becomes a “berserker” when the fighting starts, a Robin Hood-like archer, a female assassin with a dark secret etc. Even the main antagonist Ulric, the Nadir’s great war leader is a complex and honorable man. The narrative is told from both sides of the war, while we are clearly meant to be invested in the Drenai people who are under attack, the rationale of Ulric who wants to annex other nations to his own, for the sake of long-term peace and prosperity, is understandable. Gemmell was the master of plotting, pacing and —most of all—characterization. His world building is not as complex or detailed as today’s leading purveyors of epic fantasy like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/38550.Brandon_Sanderson" title="Brandon Sanderson" rel="nofollow noopener"> Brandon Sanderson</a> or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/108424.Patrick_Rothfuss" title="Patrick Rothfuss" rel="nofollow noopener"> Patrick Rothfuss</a>, the upside is that Gemmell’s books are generally much shorter. The magic side of the story is sparingly used, similar to what you would expect in an Arthurian fantasy. Gemmell was much more concerned with exploring the themes of chivalry, honor, redemption, and particularly the deeper meaning of heroism.<br><br>I feel like there is Gemmell renaissance going on just in my head. He was my single favorite fantasy author during the 80s, I don't know whether that is still the case today, or even who holds the mantle now; there are just too many great fantasy authors still working and they are quite diverse in style; it is not really worth ranking them. Sadly, David Gemmell passed away in 2006, though he left behind a considerable legacy of very well written fantasy books. The first time I read <i>Legend</i> was more than twenty years ago, I have forgotten most of the details so this is almost like a first read for me, though there are one or two highly remarkable scenes which I have never forgotten (only the context of how they come about). If you enjoy fantasy in a medieval setting but have not read any Gemmell yet you have a lot to look forward to.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1488688935i/22144243.jpg" width="400" height="120" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Notes</b>:<br>• I distinctly remember reading these Drenai books in random order during the 80s, this was before the advent of e-books, and it was hard to find all the titles in bookstores to read sequentially; so I read whatever I could find. Each novel is self-contained so there is no cliff hanger to worry about.<br><br>• That said, with e-books available now I look forward to reading them all in order. Though I would like to read his <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/43788-troy" rel="nofollow noopener">Troy series</a> which I never read before.<br><br>• Gemmell is something of a writer’s writer where the epic fantasy genre is concerned, there is even a <a href="http://www.gemmellawards.com/" rel="nofollow noopener"> David Gemmell Award</a> named after him (comparable to the Arthur C. Clarke or the Philip K. Dick awards). <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/108424.Patrick_Rothfuss" title="Patrick Rothfuss" rel="nofollow noopener"> Patrick Rothfuss</a> is a proud recipient of this award, as he mentioned <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1149888269%20" rel="nofollow noopener">in his own review</a> of this very book.<br><br><b>Quotes:</b><br><i> “What does the philosopher say of cowards and heroes?” <br>“The prophet says, ‘By nature of definition only the coward is capable of the highest heroism.’ ”<br><br>“And what is a man? He is someone who rises when life has knocked him down. He is someone who raises his fist to heaven when a storm has ruined his crop—and then plants again. And again. A man remains unbroken by the savage twists of fate.”<br><br>“That our defense will fail is no reason to avoid the battle. For it is the motive that is pure, not the outcome.”<br><br>“Yes. He is a strange one. A cynic by experience, a romantic by inclination, and now a hero by necessity.” <br><br>“Beyond the legendary armor and the eyes of icy fire, he was just another old man. Tough and strong as a bull, maybe, but old. Worn out by time, the enemy that never tired. ”</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="6297774939747041566" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
