<div id="review_72696034" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/72696034" />
    <a title="Mike (the Paladin)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2187043-mike-the-paladin"><img alt="Mike (the Paladin)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528431476p2/2187043.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/72696034?book_show_action=true">Sep 27, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mike (the Paladin)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mike (the Paladin)" href="/user/show/2187043-mike-the-paladin">Mike (the Paladin)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780099470205" href="/book/show/1741108.Legend">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2187043-mike-the-paladin?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer72696034" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8520499566769849422">The five star rating is of course a matter of taste.<br/><br/>David Gemmell is (was) one of the most gifted writers of this type of fantasy ever. It's hard to compare him to anyone else as he's sort of in a class by himself. Some compare him to Glenn Cook (whom I also like) but there are only "some" similarities. I suppose if I must come up with a "tag" I'd call Gemmell's work "heroic fantasy", sometimes "dark". While it would be incorrect to say his heroes "always" die, it is true to say that if the stor</span>
  <span id="freeText8520499566769849422" style="display:none">The five star rating is of course a matter of taste.<br /><br />David Gemmell is (was) one of the most gifted writers of this type of fantasy ever. It's hard to compare him to anyone else as he's sort of in a class by himself. Some compare him to Glenn Cook (whom I also like) but there are only "some" similarities. I suppose if I must come up with a "tag" I'd call Gemmell's work "heroic fantasy", sometimes "dark". While it would be incorrect to say his heroes "always" die, it is true to say that if the story calls for it, they do.<br /><br />Here we meet Druss (who we can find in a younger state in other writings) one of his archetypal heroes. I like Gemmell tremendously and also respect what I know of him. I found a few interviews and such with him and discovered an amazingly interesting man.<br /><br />I am going to risk a spoiler here...<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Druss and the Drenai defenders hold up in Dros Delnoch (a Drenai fortress that [of course:] has never fallen) and are (except for a few) willing and ready to defend the fort to the end (ala the Alamo, Thermopylae, etc.) In an interview Gemmell once spoke of a "reader" who wrote him and expressed a lack of understanding as to why the defenders would stay once it became obvious they couldn't hold and would be slaughtered. Gemmell said he wrote the person back and simply recommended that they not read any more of his (Gemmell's) work as if they didn't understand, he couldn't explain it to them. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Gemmell died at 58 years of age in 2006 of coronary artery disease. Many (myself among them) will miss him. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8520499566769849422" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1101413088?book_show_action=true">Nov 09, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anthony Ryan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anthony Ryan" href="/user/show/7151669-anthony-ryan">Anthony Ryan</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1101413088" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5058166146038040538">The book that really put David Gemmell on the map as an exceptional exponent of heroic fantasy. Gemmell's ability to take archetypes and depict them as real people was always one of his greatest strengths, and he succeeds admirably here. Legendary axe-wielding warrior Druss marshals a mis-matched group of Drenai to defend the mighty fortress of Dros Delnoch from the Nadir horde. All the classic Gemmell ingredients are present; gritty action, breathless pace and a depth of characterisation that h</span>
  <span id="freeText5058166146038040538" style="display:none">The book that really put David Gemmell on the map as an exceptional exponent of heroic fantasy. Gemmell's ability to take archetypes and depict them as real people was always one of his greatest strengths, and he succeeds admirably here. Legendary axe-wielding warrior Druss marshals a mis-matched group of Drenai to defend the mighty fortress of Dros Delnoch from the Nadir horde. All the classic Gemmell ingredients are present; gritty action, breathless pace and a depth of characterisation that had rarely been seen in this genre before. Whilst 'Wolf in Shadow' remains my favourite Gemmell book, for those new to his work, this may well be the best place to start.</span>

<div id="review_1927140062" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1927140062" />
    <a title="Laura" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45400990-laura"><img alt="Laura" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573825853p2/45400990.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1927140062?book_show_action=true">Jan 27, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura" href="/user/show/45400990-laura">Laura</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781857236811" href="/book/show/849768.Legend">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45400990-laura?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45400990-laura?shelf=blood-and-gore">blood-and-gore</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1927140062" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18092788085371583301"><i>
  <b>There is more to life than merely waiting for death. For life to have meaning there must be a purpose.</b>
</i><br/><br/>But what is the purpose is to die by merely prolonging the inevitable? What if you know you cannot hold? Will you still fight on? <br/><br/><i>The Drenai Empire is under threat. The tribal Nadir people have been united for the first time by the great warleader Ulric, who has forged a massive empire in the North. The Drenai leader Abalayn is trying to negotiate new treaties with Ulric, but war is brewing </i></span>
  <span id="freeText18092788085371583301" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>There is more to life than merely waiting for death. For life to have meaning there must be a purpose.</b>
</i><br><br>But what is the purpose is to die by merely prolonging the inevitable? What if you know you cannot hold? Will you still fight on? <br><br><i>The Drenai Empire is under threat. The tribal Nadir people have been united for the first time by the great warleader Ulric, who has forged a massive empire in the North. The Drenai leader Abalayn is trying to negotiate new treaties with Ulric, but war is brewing and an over 500,000 strong Nadir army marches on the fortress of Dros Delnoch, gateway to the Drenai heartlands. Dros Delnoch is the greatest fortress in the world, a narrow pass guarded by six high walls and a great keep, but under Abalayn its complement of defenders has been reduced to less than 10,000 men under the leadership of an unfit General.<br><br>The fate of the Drenai hinges on the defence of Dros Delnoch. If the fortress can hold the Nadir horde for three months, the Drenai general Magnus Woundweaver might be able to gather and train a Drenai army. However, given the odds, no-one truly believes that Delnoch can be held.<br><br>And yet there is a hope. A hope that rests on the skills of one grizzled warrior: a 60 year <b>old man with a swollen knee and arthritic back<b></b></b></i><br><br><b>Druss the Legend</b><br><br>who marches to the great fortress to defend his people one last time. He is the heart and soul of this story.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1517054163i/24944873._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>Druss the Legend by LawtonLonsdale on DeviantArt</i><br><br><b>
  <i>Druss is every man who has refused to quit; to surrender when life offered no hope; to stand aside when the alternative was to die. He is a man who has shown other men there is no such thing as guaranteed defeat. He lifts the spirit merely by being Druss, and being seen to be Druss.</i>
</b><br><br>And yet he manages to remain just a man. A man <b>
  <i>who was never mean, petty or needlessly cruel... a man who never gave in, never compromised his ideals, never betrayed a friend, never despoiled a woman and never used his strength against the weak. </i>
</b><br><br><br><b>
  <i>Get rid of your doubts. Yesterday is dead. Past mistakes are like smoke in the breeze. What counts is tomorrow and every tomorrow... </i>
</b><br><br>Lovely words, and no one can deny their truth, but how many of us actually follow them? How many of us wallow in self pity regretting the past and forgetting how to live? <br><br>This little 350 pages action jam-packed book gives us all a little well meant kick-in-the-butt and makes us think about it. It shows us that we have to value life because:<br><br><b>
  <i>You may think life is sweet now, but when death is a heartbeat away then life becomes unbearably desirable. And when you survive, everything you do will be enhanced and filled with greater joy; the sunlight, the breeze, a good wine, a woman's lips, a child's laughter. </i>
</b><br><br>To all those who'd like a fast gripping read I highly recommend this one.<br>It's <b>a hell of a story</b> and heroic fantasy at its best!<br><br>Find this review and more on my book review and cover art blog <a href="http://themagicbookcorner.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <b>The Magic Book Corner</b>
</a><br></span>

          </span>

<div id="review_2305573188" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2305573188" />
    <a title="Deborah Obida" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/54790180-deborah-obida"><img alt="Deborah Obida" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604679377p2/54790180.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2305573188?book_show_action=true">May 26, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Deborah Obida" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Deborah Obida" href="/user/show/54790180-deborah-obida">Deborah Obida</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11720877-legend">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54790180-deborah-obida?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54790180-deborah-obida?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54790180-deborah-obida?shelf=favorite-books">favorite-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2305573188" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10353484243364909354"><b>
  <i>'Liberty is only valued when it is threatened, therefore it is the threat that highlights the value.</i>
</b><br/><br/>This book exceeded my expectations, I've had this on my tbr for years and never got around to reading it till now. Legend is a classic fantasy with a dash of modernism. There are lots of battle scenes, friendship, diversity and romance. The romance is what surprised me most, I did not see that coming, it was a soul mate kind of love. The depictions of the battle scenes were awesome.<br/><br/><b>
  <i>Is my sc</i></b></span>
  <span id="freeText10353484243364909354" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>'Liberty is only valued when it is threatened, therefore it is the threat that highlights the value.</i>
</b><br /><br />This book exceeded my expectations, I've had this on my tbr for years and never got around to reading it till now. Legend is a classic fantasy with a dash of modernism. There are lots of battle scenes, friendship, diversity and romance. The romance is what surprised me most, I did not see that coming, it was a soul mate kind of love. The depictions of the battle scenes were awesome.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>Is my scar fading?'<br />Bowman peered closely at the jagged red line from brow to chin. 'You were lucky not to lose an eye,' he commented.<br />'Useless Nadir steel,' said Rek. 'I made a perfect block and his blasted sword snapped and lashed across my face. Good gods man, have you any idea how long I've protected my face?'<br />'It's too late to worry about that now,' said Bowman, grinning.<br />'Some people are born ugly,' said Rek. 'It's not their fault, and I for one have never held it against a man that he is ugly. But others - and I count myself among them - are born with handsome features. That is a gift which should not be lightly taken away.'<br />'I take it you made the perpetrator pay for his deed?'<br />'Naturally! And you know, I think he was smiling even as I slew him. But then he was an ugly man. I mean really ugly. It's not right.'</i>
</b><br /><br /><br />The world building is slightly above average, I had no issues understanding them. The writing is awesome, it's so comprehensible and fast paced. The book is written in third person multiple POV of protagonists.<br /><br />The characters though lovable didn't have enough personality, most of them were one dimensional excepting Druss, he is such an awesome character. Rek is also a good character, I wish there was more pages spent developing his character, things were kind of rushed. Same goes for Virae, Orrin and the lot of others.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>Druss is every man who has refused to quit; to surrender when life offered no hope; to stand aside when the alternative was to die. He is a man who has shown other men there is no such thing as guaranteed defeat. He lifts the spirit merely by being Druss, and being seen to be Druss.'</i>
</b><br /><br />Druss is a war hero, everyone knows his story of how he held against questionable odds till reinforcement came. He is called out of retirement to remake the miracle, he is more of a legend than a man.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>'Have you probed the man's mind?'<br />'Yes. He is a strange one. A cynic by experience, a romantic by inclination and now a hero by necessity.'</i>
</b><br /><br />The above quote is the perfect description of Rek, he doesn't like to fight though he is good at it, he is also a bersark. I didn't like that he was used, even though it paid up in the end. <br /><br />Virae is the opposite of Rek, she goes headlong into battle, she has been waiting for war all her life, when it did come she hated it. War is a terrible thing. I wish her character was more developed.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>'All things that live must die,' said Vintar. 'Man alone, it seems, lives all his life in the knowledge of death. And yet there is more to life than merely waiting for death. For life to have meaning, there must be a purpose. A man must pass something on -otherwise he is useless.</i>
</b><br /><br />The plot is actually straight forward. The people of Drenai are invaded by the Nadir king who has an army of half a million. The Drenai haven't seen war in years and have become complacent, their veterans are just 3000, they have have just 7000 recruits which consisted of farmers. The 10000 men are to hold half a million for three months before reinforcement comes. They know they have no chance but if they fail their family and their country will join the Nadir empire.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10353484243364909354" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ivan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ivan" href="/user/show/31294609-ivan">Ivan</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer934726123" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11437298494835187384">A friend here on GR asked me about short opinion of this book and if I can write something. So Agos, I hope you find this at least bit helpful.<br/><br/>It was in my early days on Goodreads I read this but my memory is still surprisingly fresh partially because in those days my number of reads per year was barely dozen or so rather than 3-digit numbers I am now managing each year.<br/><br/>Despite being written in 80's this is not Tolkien-esque fantasy but more inspired by, as name says it, legends and myths. This </span>
  <span id="freeText11437298494835187384" style="display:none">A friend here on GR asked me about short opinion of this book and if I can write something. So Agos, I hope you find this at least bit helpful.<br /><br />It was in my early days on Goodreads I read this but my memory is still surprisingly fresh partially because in those days my number of reads per year was barely dozen or so rather than 3-digit numbers I am now managing each year.<br /><br />Despite being written in 80's this is not Tolkien-esque fantasy but more inspired by, as name says it, legends and myths. This is story of heroes larger than life, great love, impossible odds on battlefield where champion meets champion. All wrapped up in warm pathos that much later Rothfuss mastered so well. <br /><br />From it's strong points comes it's weak one. Since It's inspired by legends and myths dialogues are also in that vein which makes them odd by today's standards, there is great insta-love and characters that don't even try to be realistic or plausible. There are many things like that that can be viewed as bug or feature depending on your inclinations.<br />This isn't book of rich, subtle flavors but distilled heroic fantasy.<br /><br />I for one had lot of fun. Solid 3.5 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11437298494835187384" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1212678251" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1212678251" />
    <a title="Terence" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23206148-terence"><img alt="Terence" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473945175p2/23206148.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1212678251?book_show_action=true">Feb 26, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Terence" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Terence" href="/user/show/23206148-terence">Terence</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1212678251" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12501545913540947871">An unfathomably numerous Nadir army heads to the mighty stronghold of Dros Delnoch to either accept surrender or slaughter their defenders. The old legendary warrior Druss known by many names such as Captain of the Ax, the Axman, Deathwalker, and the Silver Slayer comes to Delnoch in search of a worthy fighting death. When he arrives he realizes he can't just fight because the warriors of Dros Delnoch need him to lead.<br/><br/>Much of the tale of Legend seems to revolve around dying well. There are a lot</span>
  <span id="freeText12501545913540947871" style="display:none">An unfathomably numerous Nadir army heads to the mighty stronghold of Dros Delnoch to either accept surrender or slaughter their defenders. The old legendary warrior Druss known by many names such as Captain of the Ax, the Axman, Deathwalker, and the Silver Slayer comes to Delnoch in search of a worthy fighting death. When he arrives he realizes he can't just fight because the warriors of Dros Delnoch need him to lead.<br /><br />Much of the tale of Legend seems to revolve around dying well. There are a lot of deaths and the ones that occur in battle are honored above all others. Since the story revolves around outnumbered protagonists taking part in a siege it makes sense. With that being said the story is quite bittersweet with a mostly realistic view of the depravity and destruction of war.<br /><br />A part of the story I didn't like was the quick blazing love between Rek and Virae. I get that their is only so many pages to tell a story, but <i>everyone knows</i> if you are going to have a meet cute and want to speed up two characters falling in love then you need a montage. I guess it doesn't work the same in books as it does in 80s movies. Needless to say at this point I didn't buy Rek and Virae falling instantly in love for no real reason. That being said their relationship and devotion to one another was really well done after they fell in love.<br /><br />I also didn't like the continual shifting from one point of view character to the next without a transition or even a line break to signal a different point of view. I found it a bit frustrating, but not to the extent it kept me from reading the book.<br /><br />I really enjoyed the arthritic legend Druss. He really lived up to the legend despite being weary because of age. He is a warrior through and through and I enjoyed reading about him. For a man who insisted he was just a warrior and no leader he lead the men of Dros Delnoch admirably.<br /><br /><i>It's time for a <b>Now You Know Moment</b>. Did you know that the recurring term in Legend, baresark, is the Scandinavian term for berserker? <b>Well now you know.</b></i><br /><br />Overall I am generally dismayed to rate classic books because quite often the authors of today have borrowed from the classics and the plot points which were once uniquely spectacular now seem commonplace. I fear this was partially the case for me with Legend. Much of the story felt familiar and what made it special is unfortunately lost on me reading it 31 years later.<br /><br />2.5 out of 5 stars</span>
  <a data-text-id="12501545913540947871" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText6648676545121758718" style="display:none">This was a pretty enjoyable, straightforward fantasy. Basically, it feels like the author took the premise of the Battle of Helm's Deep (™Tolkien, LOTR) and stretched it out but the insight gained as various characters faced their own mortality was pretty interesting. Though this is marked as the first in a series it felt like a pretty self-contained story, i.e. no cliffhanger, with even a nice little epilogue to put a bow of closure on everything. </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780345913777" href="/book/show/568097.Legend">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5610133-sologdin?shelf=burns-like-cold-iron">burns-like-cold-iron</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer637322432" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2140773590287028503">Nutshell: military dilemma comes to improbable resolution through the intervention of a surly codger who kicks half million kids off lawn.<br/><br/>We know we might be in trouble on the first page with the “slanted eyes” of the foe (1). Trouble is confirmed by “the face was flat and cruel, the eyes dark and slanted” (2). Leader of the enemy is identified as “the Khan” (222).<br/><br/>This enemy is reportedly “half a million tribesmen” (20), and has “more than twice that in camp followers, cooks, engineers, and whor</span>
  <span id="freeText2140773590287028503" style="display:none">Nutshell: military dilemma comes to improbable resolution through the intervention of a surly codger who kicks half million kids off lawn.<br /><br />We know we might be in trouble on the first page with the “slanted eyes” of the foe (1). Trouble is confirmed by “the face was flat and cruel, the eyes dark and slanted” (2). Leader of the enemy is identified as “the Khan” (222).<br /><br />This enemy is reportedly “half a million tribesmen” (20), and has “more than twice that in camp followers, cooks, engineers, and whores” (80). Rather than exaggerated, this number may be “underplayed if anything […] outlying tribes were still coming in” (153). The economic system that produced this army is laid out: “the northern steppes make poor farmland. Mainly they breed goats and ponies” (160). The army is nevertheless “the greatest ever assembled, a horde that within twenty years had built an empire stretching across a dozen lands and five score cities […] the largest empire in known history” (194). In the penultimate round of bellicose braggadocio, emperor claims “I have four armies like this” (317).<br /><br />We know from Hans Delbruck, in the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1180521.Warfare_in_Antiquity_History_of_the_Art_of_War__Volume_I" title="Warfare in Antiquity History of the Art of War, Volume I by Hans Delbrück" rel="nofollow noopener">History of the Art of War Volume I Warfare in Antiquity</a>, that such army strengths transform the exceedingly improbable into manifest impossibility. Herodotus for instance gives the Persian invasion a strength of 4,200,000, including logistical components; Delbruck notes that a Prussian “corps of 30,000 men covers, in the German march order, some 14 miles, without its supply trains. The march column of the Persians would therefore have been 2,000 miles long, and when the head of the column was arriving before Thermopylae, the end of the column might have just been marching out of Susa” (loc. cit. at 35). <br /><br />In the second volume, <i>The Barbarian Invasions</i>, the professor had cause to consider, more appropriate hereto, the strengths of the Germanic invaders who broke Rome: “Even in the period of the migrations, the Germans were not very numerous, and this is only natural, since their economic conditions had remained the same. From start to finish, the Germans were principally warriors and not farmers. If they had significantly developed economically in the period, they would necessarily also have created cities. But they were still without cities […] they were primarily raisers of livestock and hunters […] Since the production of food can have increased but little, the population, too, cannot have expanded significantly […] the density of population cannot have risen importantly; it still cannot have gone far above 12 souls per square mile” (loc. cit. at 292). <br /><br />His inference is that “we may never exceed 15,000 warriors for any of the migrating tribal armies. A figure of 15,000 warriors, together with women and children, presupposes a total of at least 60,000, and with their slaves around 70,000 souls. Such a mass is already too large to move as a unit” (id. at 293).<br /><br />He concludes: “We have estimated the population of the Roman Empire toward the middle of the third century as 90 million people. […] Is it imaginable that such a large population would be overcome by attacks of barbarian hordes that were no stronger than 5,000 to 15,000 men? I believe that there can be no conclusion of greater importance in world history than that this was really the case. The legendary exaggeration in the army strengths have hidden the realization from us until now” (id.). <br /><br />Locus of confrontation in Gemmell is “the greatest fortress ever built” (195). Impossibility of army strengths notwithstanding, the stage is set therefore for the dialectical confrontation of immovable object and unstoppable force. <br /><br />The substance of the confrontation, even though it is stylistically meritorious western freedom vs. evil eastern horde, a common cold war conceit (Elric fights several undifferentiated eastern hordes, but the classical formulation is Tolkien), is southern civilization vs. northern barbarism. We might simplistically designate the former geopolitical orientation as the Germanic ideology of epic fantasy, whereas the latter is the Romanic ideology. Now that the cold war is over, fantasy is liberated from the Germanic geopolitics of Tolkien and can return to the presentation of a falling or fallen empire, as was important to the Arthurian tradition, the <i>Nibelungenlied</i>, Galfridus Monumentensis--the despair of St. Augustine ultimately. We survey the current field: Abercrombie, Morgan, Bakker, Jordan: the enemy is not the eastern horde, but rather the northern barbarian. Martin has both, maybe neutralizes both, perhaps is sui generis. Gemmell, in this text, is aesthetically Germanic but ideologically Romanic. He combines nostalgia for a dying empire with casual racism. The dying empire must defend against a northern barbarism, which without agriculture has two million soldiers under arms. It is more than impossibility. This text then might be considered a key transitional point in late cold war fantasy. <br /><br />The confrontation cooks slowly for the first two-thirds of the volume, boiling over in the final third for lots of jaw-kicking and spine-ripping. Text is marketed as a classic of military fantasy, but given the impossibilities, above, I can’t give that thesis any credibility whatsoever. Another defect in the “military fantasy” argument: eponymous surly codger’s fame is founded primarily on a Thermopylae event: “There were a few hundred Drenai warriors holding Skeln Pass while the main Drenai army massed elsewhere. […] They were outnumbered fifty to one, and they held on until reinforcements arrived. […] Gorben had an inner army of ten thousand men called the Immortals. They had never been beaten, but Druss beat them” (48).<br /><br />Turning once more to Herr Delbruck, we see that these type of pass defenses are extremely improbable (Morgan has one in the background of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3314369.The_Steel_Remains__A_Land_Fit_for_Heroes___1_" title="The Steel Remains (A Land Fit for Heroes, #1) by Richard K. Morgan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Steel Remains</a>, as I recall it): “carefully conceived strategy does not use mountains in the same way as Leonidas did for the defense of a country. Over a mountain range […] there is always more than one route […] It is hard to occupy all of them, and one can never succeed in defending them all. The enemy will always find a place […] Once the line is penetrated at one place, then the garrisons of all the other passes are endangered” (<i>Warfare in Antiquity</i> at 92). <br /><br />So, yeah, not persuasive. If the text is important (and I think it is), then it is important for its transformational position, the knife’s edge on the Romanic/Germanic orientation: the immovable object of Tolkien’s cold war orientation broken by the unstoppable force of Romanic nostalgia. <br /><br />Marred overall by improbable narrative development, generic setting development, lack of perspective discipline, and a generalized cheesiness.<br /><br />Recommended for those who believe that <i>you son of a slut</i> is a useful pejorative, persons who stand at a frozen moment of history, and readers who feel the strange sense of departure that heralds the baresark rage.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2140773590287028503" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6664463849314389393">After a disastrous start, when I almost abandoned it, I ended up liking it a lot. <br/><br/>Even if I’m not a fan of military fantasy, the battle here was a great experience. However, the love story intertwined with the war is the worst I have read so far, but I guess Gemmel’s intention was to show that love prevails no matter what. <br/><br/>Druss, Serbitar, Hogun, Gilad, Orrin, Bowman, even Ulric – I loved them all. Rek and Virae not. But I can’t help wondering if there’s more to the two of them, because all othe</span>
  <span id="freeText6664463849314389393" style="display:none">After a disastrous start, when I almost abandoned it, I ended up liking it a lot. <br /><br />Even if I’m not a fan of military fantasy, the battle here was a great experience. However, the love story intertwined with the war is the worst I have read so far, but I guess Gemmel’s intention was to show that love prevails no matter what. <br /><br />Druss, Serbitar, Hogun, Gilad, Orrin, Bowman, even Ulric – I loved them all. Rek and Virae not. But I can’t help wondering if there’s more to the two of them, because all other characters are so well developed. The preparation for battle and the war itself are masterfully written. The imagery is so vivid that I cringed and felt pain reading the battle scenes. And if you think GRRM is a butcher, then you haven’t met Gemmel…<br /><br />The battle itself steals the show and I couldn’t put the book down after its second half. But I would have loved some worldbuilding too, for there is none. Plus, there are two dei ex machina moments which made me roll my eyes. <br /><br />Nonetheless, the battle scenes, the interaction between the characters during these scenes, the humorous dialogues on occasion made this story to be a very enjoyable one, albeit I don’t think I will read another in this series, because everything <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[(and everyone I cared about) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> burned out here. This should have been the third in a trilogy, not the first.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9120370270886207412">Great heroic fantasy! I really liked Gemmel's writing style, great characterization, and enthralling battle scenes. It's a really strong book, absolutely a book to remember.<br/>Highly recommended !!!<br/><br/>5/5</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_110934240" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/110934240" />
    <a title="Dawn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2517340-dawn"><img alt="Dawn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1480301169p2/2517340.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/110934240?book_show_action=true">Jul 10, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dawn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dawn" href="/user/show/2517340-dawn">Dawn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780099470205" href="/book/show/1741108.Legend">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2517340-dawn?shelf=read-in-2012">read-in-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2517340-dawn?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer110934240" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4524916594448956165">Where do I even begin? I just don't get it. I don't get the praise for this book, I don't get the four and five star ratings... I just don't get it.<br/><br/>It's just so stuffed with awful, it's overflowing. It's lucky to be getting two stars from me.. If not for a few (very few) redeeming sections that I actually enjoyed, it wouldn't even pull that. But I mean honestly. Really? Really really?<br/><br/>I don't even know where to start. I mean Rek.. He was just so inconsistent. He's described one way when we meet h</span>
  <span id="freeText4524916594448956165" style="display:none">Where do I even begin? I just don't get it. I don't get the praise for this book, I don't get the four and five star ratings... I just don't get it.<br /><br />It's just so stuffed with awful, it's overflowing. It's lucky to be getting two stars from me.. If not for a few (very few) redeeming sections that I actually enjoyed, it wouldn't even pull that. But I mean honestly. Really? Really really?<br /><br />I don't even know where to start. I mean Rek.. He was just so inconsistent. He's described one way when we meet him, but his actions never fit that description, and just get further and further from it as the story progresses. Not in a character development type way.. Just in a what the fuck kind of way. Druss.. Whatever, he was ok I guess, but nothing special. All of the characters in general were just ok. I did like Orrin, but that's about it.<br /><br />The dialogue.. Oh my good God the dialogue. It's so horrible and awkward and unrealistic, it physically hurt me to read it. The relationships and bonds formed between characters felt totally contrived. It was just bad. So so bad.<br /><br />The romance.. So fucking weird. Anyone who has read this knows the relationship I'm talking about. It was just... Creepy to me. Like tie-a-chick-up-in-a-closet-and-cut-off-all-of-her-fingers-and-feed-them-to-her-one-by-one creepy. And don't even get me started on how the women in this book are treated! In one scene, a husband straight up punches his wife in the face during a disagreement. She asks him later if he's going to apologize, and he's basically like "bitch, please..." and kisses her to make it all better. And that's ok with her. Later a woman is sternly told to "OBEY YOUR HUSBAND, WOMAN!" and she meekly does. It's just.. It's like Gemmell never met an actual woman. And before you say anything.. I get it. It's fantasy. It's an alternate world, maybe that's just the culture, right? But it didn't feel like that. It just felt.. Wrong.<br /><br />I had been warned though, about the dialogue issues and the women issues. But I was assured that Gemmell was the master of Sword and Sorcery type fantasy, and that his battles more than made up for it. So I waited.. Battle time came.. It was fine I guess, but nothing spectacular. I guess maybe when it's written beside that horrible dialogue, you're just glad they're done talking, so it becomes better in comparison? I don't know. I honestly don't. For me, just fine wasn't nearly enough to make up for all of the crap.<br /><br />I could go on.. But it's pointless. Obviously I just don't get it. I really wanted to like this, I wanted to love it in fact. But I couldn't. Even trying my hardest, I couldn't. I probably will read another book in this series, just to see if maybe it will hook me. I do really want to like it.. And I understand that this was Gemmell's first book.. Maybe it gets better. Maybe I'll read another, get hooked, and then my opinion on this will improve. It wouldn't be the first time! But for now.. Two stars. Barely.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4524916594448956165" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_396025606" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/396025606" />
    <a title="Kristalia " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5705623-kristalia"><img alt="Kristalia " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1535637983p2/5705623.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/396025606?book_show_action=true">Aug 20, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristalia " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristalia " href="/user/show/5705623-kristalia">Kristalia </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">all people who love tragic, beautiful and great story of a town under a  siege </span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=own-physical-copy">own-physical-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=unique-or-different-story">unique-or-different-story</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=favorites-absolute">favorites-absolute</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=favorite-couple">favorite-couple</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=cut-my-heart-out">cut-my-heart-out</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=why-u-no-longer-u-make-me-sad">why-u-no-longer-u-make-me-sad</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=6-stars">6-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=type-standalone-story">type-standalone-story</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=favorite-series">favorite-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer396025606" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer272214812531064170"><b>Final rating: 6/5 stars</b><br/><br/> <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380388327i/748722.png' width='400' height='220' alt='legend' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>1. This book is LEGEND-wait for it-DARYYYYYYYYYYYY!<br/>2. Seriously, one of the best books i have ever read.<br/>3. The book which is officially my 300th read one.<br/>4. The type of book which i always wanted to read.<br/>5. The one that i will never regret buying.<br/>6. And the one which made me cry like a baby.<br/>7. Look at that unresistable Serbian edition cover which i own:<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380388327i/748723.jpg' width='310' alt='look at that beautiful cover!!!!' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>Isn't it beautiful?<br/><br/>Now, i have read a lot of high/epic fantasy and i love many authors like Jordan and Martin. All of th</span>
  <span id="freeText272214812531064170" style="display:none"><b>Final rating: 6/5 stars</b><br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380388327i/748722.png" width="400" height="220" alt="legend" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>1. This book is LEGEND-wait for it-DARYYYYYYYYYYYY!<br>2. Seriously, one of the best books i have ever read.<br>3. The book which is officially my 300th read one.<br>4. The type of book which i always wanted to read.<br>5. The one that i will never regret buying.<br>6. And the one which made me cry like a baby.<br>7. Look at that unresistable Serbian edition cover which i own:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380388327i/748723.jpg" width="310" alt="look at that beautiful cover!!!!" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Isn't it beautiful?<br><br>Now, i have read a lot of high/epic fantasy and i love many authors like Jordan and Martin. All of their series are full of magic, mythical beings, races and elements of High fantasy.<br><br>After i read this book i can place David Gemmmell as one of my fav authors and this book in my favorites. <br><br>Legend is different. It has little magic, and the magic it has is unique and interesting. The story is more about siege of Dros Delnoch. It has everything i love, siege, strategy, drama, romance, great characters and loving couples. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b><br> “Why now? Why not? Live or die, a man and a woman need love. There is a need in the race. We need to share. To belong. Perhaps you will die before the year is out. But remember this: to have may be taken from you, to have had never. Far better to have tasted love before dying, than to die alone.” <br></b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br>While we are at drama, i cried last 200 pages of the book, so thank god i didn't destroy it with my tears....<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>► CHARACTERS:</b>
</blockquote><br><br>There are many characters and they all get special place in the book. We find a lot about them, their lives, their pasts, and they are all deep characters which you will love.<br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b><br>“By nature of definition only the coward is capable of the highest heroism” <br></b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>There is also romance between Rek and Virae. They were sweet and loving couple. I enjoyed every moment of their romance :D<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>► OVERALL:</b>
</blockquote><br><br>The ending was great, and the book can be read standalone but i will certainly read other books as well, because David Gemmell proved to be Legend as much as this book is. <br><br><u>
  <i>
    <b>What i liked: </b>
  </i>
</u><br>☑ war strategies<br>☑ the construction of Dros Delnoch<br>☑ The magic System<br>☑ That the magic was not the main point in the book<br>☑ I loved <i>all</i> the characters, including women which rarely happens<br>☑ I loved how David Gemmell made the characters deep, revealed their pasts and made POVs with different people.<br>☑ I especially love how the book ended <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ With Rek and company going to the Nadir party before the end  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br>☑ I loved the romance (Gemmell didn't over do it) and besides they were a cute couple <br>☑ and all the drama (MAJOR SPOILER <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ especially when Virae and Serbitar died <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> )<br><br><u>
  <i>
    <b>what i DIDN'T like: </b>
  </i>
</u><br>☒ hm....now that i think of it, there was nothing i didn't like.... This book is perfect in every way.<br><br>Now, excuse me while i go to cry again :(<br><br>Edit 04. Dec. 2015: Looking back at this review, I am sad that I didn't write much more detailed review for it. Because of this I will have to sit down one day, reread the book and write a new version of my review.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>► REVIEW(S) RELATED TO THIS BOOK:</b>
</blockquote><br><br>◈ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/396025606" rel="nofollow noopener"> Legend (Drenai Saga, #1) </a> <br>◈ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/396025634" rel="nofollow noopener"> Waylander (Drenai Saga, #3) </a><br>◈ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/396025644" rel="nofollow noopener"> Quest for Lost Heroes (The Drenai Saga, #4) </a></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Hw6vpsu1dZE8IWmphs91/YgIrDf2phZWdMfkO/diaSEGe48eQORQZbW7pQ3CLv/QRBq1WOeTuoYH1NeHkjiI/g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('BYBGutPW8F6hI2kt3GO/apGSaYh1Umq8CWlz5e9kk8sc9WYCWIfVqii5pYmYgjVHXYBw52Rnxmx6ekBZij5yFA==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer14345640734721996807">David Andrew Gemmell was a bestselling British author of heroic fantasy. A former journalist and newspaper editor, Gemmell had his first work of fiction published in 1984. He went on to write over thirty novels. Best known for his debut, Legend, Gemmell's works display violence, yet also explores themes in honour, loyalty and redemption. With over one million copies sold, his work continues to sel</span>
  <span id="freeText14345640734721996807" style="display:none">David Andrew Gemmell was a bestselling British author of heroic fantasy. A former journalist and newspaper editor, Gemmell had his first work of fiction published in 1984. He went on to write over thirty novels. Best known for his debut, Legend, Gemmell's works display violence, yet also explores themes in honour, loyalty and redemption. With over one million copies sold, his work continues to sell worldwide.</span>

        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]>
</script>
